# LoCoBench-Agent Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: javascript_web_social_expert_073_architectural_understanding_expert_01
**Category**: architectural_understanding
**Difficulty**: expert
**Language**: javascript
**Context Length**: 739599 tokens
**Files**: 87

## Task Title

Analyze Performance Bottleneck in Asynchronous User Progress Update Flow

## Description

The PulseLearn Campus Hub is a complex, microservices-based e-learning platform. The architecture leverages event-driven patterns using Kafka to ensure services are loosely coupled and scalable, as detailed in the project's Architectural Decision Records (ADRs). Recently, users have reported a significant and intermittent delay: after they complete a course lecture or quiz, it can sometimes take up to a minute for their progress to be reflected on their main dashboard's progress chart and activity stream. This delay is causing user frustration and appears to worsen during peak usage hours. As an expert architect, you need to analyze the system to identify the likely cause of this latency.

## Your Task

Your task is to perform a root cause analysis of the user progress update latency. You must not write or modify any code. Instead, produce a detailed architectural analysis report in markdown format. 

The report must:
1.  **Trace the complete, end-to-end data flow.** Start from the user's action in the frontend (e.g., completing a lecture in `LecturePlayer.js`), through the API Gateway, to all relevant backend services, and finally back to the frontend components that display the progress (`ProgressChart.js`, `ActivityStream.js`). Clearly distinguish between synchronous API calls and asynchronous event-driven messages.
2.  **Identify the key architectural components involved.** List the specific services, databases, message brokers, and critical code modules (e.g., controllers, services, repositories, event producers/consumers) that participate in this flow.
3.  **Pinpoint the top 3 most likely architectural areas causing the delay.** For each potential bottleneck, provide a detailed justification referencing specific files (e.g., `docker-compose.yml`, `nginx.conf`, service code, or ADRs) and architectural patterns (e.g., eventual consistency, producer/consumer configuration) that support your hypothesis.

## Expected Approach

An expert developer would approach this by systemically tracing the data flow and reasoning about the system's design trade-offs.

1.  **Start at the UI:** Examine `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` and its child components like `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` to see how they fetch data. This will likely lead to `frontend/src/services/courseService.js` or a similar client.
2.  **Trace the 'Write' Path:** Hypothesize that completing a lecture triggers a POST/PUT request. Look in `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` for an API call that updates progress.
3.  **Follow to the Backend:** Trace this API call through the `services/api-gateway/nginx.conf` to its destination, the `course-service`.
4.  **Analyze the Core Service Logic:** Inside `course-service`, inspect the relevant controller (`courseController.js`), service (`courseService.js`), and repository (`courseRepository.js`) to see how the progress update is persisted to its database (`schema.prisma`).
5.  **Identify the Asynchronous Link:** Crucially, the developer must consult the documentation, specifically `docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md`, to understand that cross-service communication happens via events. They would then look for an event being published in `course-service` after the database write, likely in `services/course-service/src/events/producer.js`.
6.  **Analyze the 'Read' Path:** Return to the dashboard components. How do they get the updated data? They likely poll the `course-service` periodically for the latest progress. The delay is the time between the 'write' action and the next successful 'read' poll that reflects the new data.
7.  **Synthesize Bottlenecks:** The 'intermittent' and 'under load' nature of the problem strongly points away from simple synchronous code and towards the asynchronous messaging system or infrastructure contention. The expert would identify Kafka as the most likely source of variable delay. They would formulate hypotheses based on common failure modes in event-driven systems: producer performance, broker load, and consumer lag. They would also consider the frontend polling strategy as a contributor to perceived latency.

## Evaluation Criteria

- **Flow Tracing Accuracy:** Correctly identifies and separates the synchronous write, asynchronous event, and frontend read paths.
- **Component Identification:** Accurately lists the critical services, infrastructure, and specific files involved in the process.
- **Evidence-Based Reasoning:** Cites specific files (`docker-compose.yml`, ADRs, service code) to justify conclusions.
- **Problem Diagnosis:** Correctly identifies the asynchronous, event-driven nature of the architecture (`eventual consistency`) as the root cause of the *type* of delay.
- **Bottleneck Plausibility:** Proposes at least two plausible, architecturally-sound bottlenecks (e.g., Kafka contention, frontend polling, DB load).
- **Understanding of Trade-offs:** Demonstrates an understanding that this latency is a trade-off inherent in the chosen loosely-coupled, event-driven architecture.

84-assistanttool_useRead
85-usertool_resultRead
     1→<!--
     2→  ADR 003: Polyglot Persistence
     3→  PulseLearn Campus Hub
     4→  Status: Accepted
     5→  Date: 2024-05-28
     6→-->
     7→
     8→# 003 – Polyglot Persistence  
     9→
    10→## Status  
    11→Accepted – The decision has been implemented in `v1.4.0`.
    12→
    13→## Context  
    14→PulseLearn Campus Hub is an event-driven system with a variety of read/write patterns:
    15→
    16→* Write-intensive, append-only domain events (≈8 k eps peak)  
    17→* Read-heavy social timelines that must fan-out to thousands of users in < 150 ms  
    18→* Strongly-consistent, relational data for billing, LMS compliance, and audit logs  
    19→* Full-text search over course content and peer-review comments  
    20→* Graph-style traversals for cohort relationships and content recommendations
    21→
    22→A single storage engine cannot optimize for all these needs without unacceptable trade-offs in performance, cost, or developer productivity. We therefore evaluated several strategies:
    23→
    24→| Option | Pros | Cons |
    25→| ------ | ---- | ---- |
    26→| 1. Single SQL RDBMS (PostgreSQL) | ACID, mature tooling | Hot partitions, expensive scaling, poor search |
    27→| 2. Single document DB (MongoDB) | Flexible schema, good read scaling | Event ordering issues, multi-doc transactions slower |
    28→| 3. Polyglot persistence *(selected)* | Fit-for-purpose stores, cost-effective | Operational complexity, cross-store transactions |
    29→
    30→## Decision  
    31→We adopt **polyglot persistence**: each bounded context chooses the persistence technology that best serves its needs, within guardrails enforced by the Platform Team.
    32→
    33→1. **Event Store**  
    34→   *Technology:* Apache Kafka (log), TimescaleDB (cold storage)  
 
... (truncated)

     1→```markdown
     2→# PulseLearn Campus Hub – **web_social**
     3→
     4→[![CI](https://github.com/pulselearn/campus-hub/actions/workflows/ci.yml/badge.svg)](https://github.com/pulselearn/campus-hub/actions/workflows/ci.yml)
     5→[![Coverage Status](https://coveralls.io/repos/github/pulselearn/campus-hub/badge.svg?branch=main)](https://coveralls.io/github/pulselearn/campus-hub?branch=main)
     6→[![License: MIT](https://img.shields.io/badge/License-MIT-yellow.svg)](LICENSE)
     7→
     8→PulseLearn Campus Hub transforms any educational institution into a real-time digital campus.  
     9→Students, teachers, and administrators collaborate through activity streams that react instantly to learning events such as lecture uploads, quiz completions, or peer-review feedback.  
    10→
    11→<details>

I have completed the architectural analysis. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Analysis Summary

I traced the complete end-to-end data flow for user progress updates in the PulseLearn Campus Hub microservices architecture and identified **3 key architectural bottlenecks** causing the reported 30-60 second latency:

### Top 3 Bottlenecks Identified:

1. **Single Kafka Broker with No Partitioning** (Highest Probability)
   - The `docker-compose.yml` shows a single-broker Kafka deployment with `KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1`
   - Under peak load (8k events/sec per ADR-003), consumer lag accumulates
   - Fire-and-forget error handling in `courseService.js:91` means failed events are lost

2. **Eventual Consistency and 60-Second Cache TTL**
   - Course data cached for 60 seconds in Redis (`courseService.js:101-109`)
   - Cache invalidation patterns may not cover all read paths
   - Progress aggregation handled by separate projection consumers with their own lag

3. **Frontend WebSocket Reliability Issues**
   - Dashboard makes a single REST call on mount, then relies entirely on WebSocket
   - No periodic polling fallback when WebSocket disconnects
   - Three independent WebSocket connections with separate reconnection logic (up to 30s backoff)

### Key Insight:

The delays are **intermittent** and **worsen under load** because this is the expected behavior of the documented eventual consistency architecture. The ADRs explicitly acknowledge these trade-offs—the architecture prioritizes service autonomy and fault isolation over strong consistency guarantees.

The solution has been written to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with complete data flow traces, component identification, and evidence-based analysis referencing specific files and line numbers.

System-Level Diagram\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    subgraph Browser / Mobile\n        A[SPA<br/>(React/Next.js)]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Edge\n        AGW[API Gateway<br/>(Node.js + Fastify)]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Core Services\n        Auth[Auth Service]\n        Users[User Service]\n        Courses[Course Service]\n        Events[Event Dispatcher]\n        Notif[Notification Service]\n        Reco[Recommendation Service]\n        Search[Search Indexer]\n    end\n\n    subgraph Infra\n        Kafka[(Kafka/NATS)]\n        DB[(PostgreSQL)]\n        Redis[(Redis)]\n        S3[(Object Storage)]\n        Prom[(Prometheus + Grafana)]\n    end\n\n    A -- REST/WebSocket --> AGW\n    AGW -- JWT --> Auth\n    AGW -- RPC --> Users & Courses\n    AGW -- Publish Domain Events --> Kafka\n    Kafka --> Events\n    Events --> Notif & Reco & Search\n    DB <--> Users & Courses\n    Redis <--> Notif\n    S3 <--> Courses\n    Prom --> Grafana\n```\n\n---\n\n## 2. Layered Component Model\n\n| Layer             | Responsibility                                  | Protocols                           |\n| ----------------- | ----------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------- |\n| Presentation      | React SPA, WebSocket client, SSR pages          | `HTTPS`, `WSS`                      |\n| API Gateway       | Rate-limit, authN, authZ, request enrichment    | `HTTP/2`, `gRPC` (internal)         |\n| Service Layer     | Business logic, orchestration, validation       | `gRPC`, `Kafka`                     |\n| Repository Layer  | Data mappers, ORM (Prisma), caching             | `SQL`, `Redis`                      |\n| Event Backbone    | Guaranteed, ordered domain event propagation    | `Kafka`, `NATS JetStream`           |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Technology Stack\n\n| Concern            | Choice                         | Rationale                                              |\n| ------------------ | ------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------ |\n| Runtime            | Node.js (v18 LTS)              | Native ESM, top-level `await`, diagnostics channel     |\n| Web Framework      | Fastify (4.x)                  | High-performance, schema-driven, hooks                 |\n| ORM                | Prisma (5.x)                   | Type-safe, migrations as code                          |\n| Message Bus        | Kafka (3.x) / NATS (2.x)       | At-least-once delivery, back-pressure control          |\n| Auth               | Clerk (OIDC) + JWT             | Social logins, MFA, SSO                                |\n| Observability      | OpenTelemetry + Prometheus     | Distributed tracing & metrics                          |\n| Containerization   | Docker + Helm                  | K8s ready, GitOps deploys                              |\n| CI/CD              | GitHub Actions, Renovate       | SemVer releases, automated dependency updates          |\n\n---\n\n## 4. Domain Event Contract (TypeScript)\n\n```ts\n/**\n * Base interface for all domain events.\n * Each event must be serializable and contain a unique ID\n * to guarantee idempotent consumption by downstream services.\n */\nexport interface DomainEvent<T extends Record<string, unknown> = unknown> {\n  readonly id: string;                  // ULID\n  readonly name: string;                // e.g. \"AssignmentSubmitted\"\n  readonly occurredAt: string;          // ISO-8601 timestamp\n  readonly aggregateId: string;         // Entity root ID (e.g. assignmentId)\n  readonly payload: T;                  // Raw event data\n  readonly version: number;             // Schema evolution support\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Event Emitter (Service \u279c Kafka)\n\n```ts\nimport { Kafka, Producer } from \"kafkajs\";\nimport { DomainEvent } from \"../types/events\";\n\nexport class EventEmitter {\n  private readonly producer: Producer;\n\n  constructor(private readonly kafka: Kafka) {\n    this.producer = kafka.producer({ allowAutoTopicCreation: false });\n  }\n\n  async start(): Promise<void> {\n    await this.producer.connect();\n  }\n\n  async stop(): Promise<void> {\n    await this.producer.disconnect();\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Publish a domain event to the message bus.\n   * Retries are handled by kafkajs with exponential back-off.\n   */\n  async emit(event: DomainEvent): Promise<void> {\n    await this.producer.send({\n      topic: `domain.${event.name}`,\n      messages: [\n        {\n          key: event.aggregateId,\n          value: JSON.stringify(event),\n          headers: { \"x-event-version\": `${event.version}` },\n        },\n      ],\n    });\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 6. Event Consumer Skeleton\n\n```ts\nimport { Kafka, EachMessagePayload } from \"kafkajs\";\nimport { logger } from \"../utils/logger\";\nimport { processAssignmentSubmitted } from \"./handlers/assignmentSubmitted\";\n\nconst TOPIC = \"domain.AssignmentSubmitted\";\n\nexport async function createAssignmentSubmittedConsumer(kafka: Kafka) {\n  const consumer = kafka.consumer({ groupId: \"notification-service\" });\n\n  await consumer.subscribe({ topic: TOPIC, fromBeginning: false });\n\n  await consumer.run({\n    autoCommit: false,\n    eachMessage: async (payload: EachMessagePayload) => {\n      try {\n        const { message, heartbeat, commitOffsetsIfNecessary } = payload;\n        const event = JSON.parse(message.value!.toString());\n\n        await processAssignmentSubmitted(event);\n\n        await commitOffsetsIfNecessary();\n        await heartbeat(); // keep consumer session alive\n      } catch (error) {\n        logger.error(error, \"Failed to process AssignmentSubmitted\");\n        // Optionally forward to a dead-letter topic for inspection\n      }\n    },\n  });\n\n  return consumer;\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 7. Repository Pattern (Prisma + Caching)\n\n```ts\nimport { PrismaClient, User } from \"@prisma/client\";\nimport Redis from \"ioredis\";\nimport ms from \"ms\";\n\nexport class UserRepository {\n  private readonly cacheTtl = ms(\"10m\") / 1000; // seconds\n\n  constructor(\n    private readonly prisma: PrismaClient,\n    private readonly redis: Redis\n  ) {}\n\n  private cacheKey(userId: string): string {\n    return `user:${userId}`;\n  }\n\n  async findById(userId: string): Promise<User | null> {\n    // 1. Check Redis\n    const cached = await this.redis.get(this.cacheKey(userId));\n    if (cached) return JSON.parse(cached) as User;\n\n    // 2. Fallback to DB\n    const user = await this.prisma.user.findUnique({ where: { id: userId } });\n    if (user) {\n      await this.redis.set(\n        this.cacheKey(userId),\n        JSON.stringify(user),\n        \"EX\",\n        this.cacheTtl\n      );\n    }\n    return user;\n  }\n\n  async create(data: Omit<User, \"id\">): Promise<User> {\n    const user = await this.prisma.user.create({ data });\n    await this.redis.del(this.cacheKey(user.id)); // bust cache\n    return user;\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 8. Example Service (Notification Service)\n\n```ts\nimport { EventEmitter } from \"../events/eventEmitter\";\nimport { NotificationRepository } from \"../repositories/notificationRepo\";\nimport { DomainEvent } from \"../types/events\";\n\nexport class NotificationService {\n  constructor(\n    private readonly repo: NotificationRepository,\n    private readonly emitter: EventEmitter\n  ) {}\n\n  /**\n   * Create a user notification and emit a follow-up domain event.\n   */\n  async notify(event: DomainEvent<AssignmentPayload>): Promise<void> {\n    // Business invariant\n    if (!event.payload.recipientId) {\n      throw new Error(\"Recipient ID missing in AssignmentSubmitted event\");\n    }\n\n    const notification = await this.repo.create({\n      userId: event.payload.recipientId,\n      title: \"New Assignment Submitted\",\n      body: `${event.payload.authorName} has submitted an assignment.`,\n    });\n\n    await this.emitter.emit({\n      id: crypto.randomUUID(),\n      name: \"NotificationCreated\",\n      occurredAt: new Date().toISOString(),\n      aggregateId: notification.id,\n      payload: { notificationId: notification.id },\n      version: 1,\n    });\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 9. Security Considerations\n\n1. **JWT validation** is enforced at the API Gateway with public JWK rotation every 60 minutes.  \n2. **TLS 1.3** is mandatory for all edge traffic; internal traffic uses mTLS between micro-services.  \n3. **CSP, HSTS, and CSRF** protection headers set by Fastify `helmet` plugin.  \n4. **OPA-based policy engine** scopes admin operations (audit logs, PII access).  \n\n---\n\n## 10. Observability Pipeline\n\n```mermaid\nsequenceDiagram\n    participant Svc as Micro-Service\n    participant OT as OpenTelemetry SDK\n    participant OTEL as OpenTelemetry Collector\n    participant Prom as Prometheus\n    participant Loki as Grafana Loki\n\n    Svc->>OT: traceSpan.start()\n    OT->>OTEL: gRPC (OTLP) export\n    OTEL->>Prom: metrics\n    OTEL->>Loki: logs\n    Prom-->>Grafana: scrape + dashboards\n```\n\nKey SLOs  \n\u2022 P99 API latency < 150 ms  \n\u2022 Event delivery success \u2265 99.999%  \n\u2022 Uptime \u2265 99.95%\n\n---\n\n## 11. Deployment Workflow\n\n1. Push to `main` triggers GitHub Action.  \n2. Lint, test, build Docker image tagged as `sha`.  \n3. Image pushed to GHCR, Helm chart updated with image sha.  \n4. ArgoCD auto-syncs chart to staging cluster.  \n5. End-to-end Cypress tests run inside cluster.  \n6. Manual approval gate promotes to production.\n\n---\n\n## 12. Glossary\n\n| Term                 | Meaning                                         |\n| -------------------- | ----------------------------------------------- |\n| Domain Event         | Immutable fact about something that happened    |\n| Aggregate            | Consistency boundary around a domain entity     |\n| CQRS                 | Command Query Responsibility Segregation        |\n| SAGA                 | Long-running transaction pattern                |\n\n---\n\n> \u00a9 PulseLearn, Inc.   "file": {
    "content": "```markdown\n# ADR-002: Introduce Event Sourcing with Kafka\n\n* Status: **Accepted**  \n* Date: 2024-05-13  \n* Decision Makers: Core Platform Team (PulseLearn Campus Hub)  \n* Supersedes: *N/A*  \n* References: PCH-RFC-11, ADR-001 (Adopt Micro-Service Architecture)  \n\n---\n\n## 1. Context \u2011 Why change?\n\nPulseLearn Campus Hub (PCH) is experiencing rapid feature growth:\n\n* Real-time dashboards for quiz progress, peer-review feedback, and badge awards  \n* A new gamification engine that recalculates points on every learning event  \n* Audit-ready reporting for compliance and accreditation bodies  \n\nThe existing CRUD-centric model has hit several limits:\n\n| Pain-Point                          | Symptom                                                                             |\n|------------------------------------|-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------|\n| Data-coupling                       | Multiple bounded contexts write to the same tables, causing noisy merge conflicts. |\n| Missed notifications                | Lost WebSocket messages because they were dispatched directly from HTTP handlers.   |\n| Operational complexity              | Replaying history (e.g., to debug ranking errors) requires fragile SQL scripts.     |\n| Lack of temporal data               | Hard to answer \u201cWhat was Alice\u2019s score at 14:01 yesterday?\u201d                         |\n\nTo address these, we want:\n\n1. **Immutable event log** \u2013 the single source of truth  \n2. **Replayability** \u2013 rebuild read-models at any point in time  \n3. **Loose coupling** \u2013 services subscribe to what they need, when they need it  \n4. **Scalability** \u2013 horizontal partitioning of event streams  \n\nApache **Kafka** is already used in our data-analytics pipeline; adopting it as the system event backbone is a natural next step.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Decision\n\nWe will adopt **event sourcing** for all new domain workflows and gradually migrate existing ones.  \nKafka will act as the **persistent event store** (commit log) and **message bus**.  \nSpecifics:\n\n1. **Each bounded context owns its topic(s)** \u2013 e.g. `education.assignment`, `identity.session`, `gamification.badge`.\n2. **Events are immutable** JSON messages, versioned via a `schemaVersion` field; schema registry enforced at the gateway.\n3. **Append-only**: write operations emit events; read models are derived via consumer projections.\n4. **Exactly-once** semantics: achieved by Kafka idempotent producers + transactional writes to outbox tables when necessary.\n5. **Snapshot strategy**: Long-lived aggregates publish `*.snapshot` events every *n* revisions to shorten replay time.\n6. **Backward compatibility**: Services must ignore unknown fields and can only add optional fields to existing event versions.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Consequences\n\nPositive:\n\n* **Auditability** \u2013 every state change is traceable.  \n* **Resilience** \u2013 consumers can restart and replay without data loss.  \n* **Scalable read models** \u2013 each service builds its own query-optimized projection.  \n\nNegative / Trade-offs:\n\n* **Write complexity** \u2013 commands must succeed or be compensated by new events.  \n* **Learning curve** \u2013 developers must understand eventual consistency.  \n* **Storage cost** \u2013 Kafka cluster size grows with retained history.  \n\n---\n\n## 4. Implementation Sketch (JavaScript / Node.js)\n\nBelow are cut-down excerpts from production code to guide contributors.  \nAll examples assume Node.js \u2265 18, TypeScript, and the `kafkajs` client.\n\n### 4.1 Common Infrastructure\n\n```ts\n// src/infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient.ts\nimport { Kafka, logLevel } from 'kafkajs';\nimport config from '../../config';\n\nexport const kafka = new Kafka({\n  clientId: 'pulselearn-campus-hub',\n  brokers : config.kafka.brokers,\n  ssl     : true,\n  sasl    : {\n    mechanism : 'scram-sha-256',\n    username  : config.kafka.username,\n    password  : config.kafka.password,\n  },\n  logLevel: logLevel.WARN,\n});\n\nexport function topicName(boundedContext: string, suffix = ''): string {\n  return `${config.env}.${boundedContext}${suffix && `.${suffix}`}`;\n}\n```\n\n### 4.2 Event Contracts\n\n```ts\n// src/domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent.ts\nimport { z } from 'zod';\n\nexport const AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema = z.object({\n  schemaVersion  : z.literal(1),\n  eventId        : z.string().uuid(),\n  aggregateId    : z.string().uuid(),   // Assignment ID\n  type           : z.literal('AssignmentSubmitted'),\n  occurredAt     : z.string().datetime({ offset: true }),\n  payload        : z.object({\n    courseId  : z.string().uuid(),\n    studentId : z.string().uuid(),\n    fileUrl   : z.string().url(),\n  }),\n});\n\nexport type AssignmentSubmittedEvent = z.infer<typeof AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema>;\n```\n\n### 4.3 Producer (Command Handler -> Event)\n\n```ts\n// src/application/commands/submitAssignment.ts\nimport { AssignmentSubmittedEvent } from '../../domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent';\nimport { kafka, topicName } from '../../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\nimport { randomUUID } from 'crypto';\n\nexport async function submitAssignment(cmd: {\n  courseId: string;\n  studentId: string;\n  fileUrl: string;\n}): Promise<void> {\n  // Business validation omitted for brevity\n\n  const event: AssignmentSubmittedEvent = {\n    schemaVersion : 1,\n    eventId       : randomUUID(),\n    aggregateId   : randomUUID(),\n    type          : 'AssignmentSubmitted',\n    occurredAt    : new Date().toISOString(),\n    payload       : cmd,\n  };\n\n  const producer = kafka.producer({ idempotent: true });\n  await producer.connect();\n\n  try {\n    await producer.send({\n      topic: topicName('education.assignment'),\n      messages: [\n        {\n          key  : event.aggregateId,\n          value: JSON.stringify(event),\n          headers: {\n            'schema-version': '1',\n            'event-type'    : event.type,\n          },\n        },\n      ],\n    });\n  } finally {\n    await producer.disconnect();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### 4.4 Consumer Projection (Gamification Points)\n\n```ts\n// src/projections/gamification/pointsProjector.ts\nimport { kafka, topicName } from '../../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\nimport { AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema } from '../../domain/events/AssignmentSubmittedEvent';\nimport pointsRepo from '../../repositories/pointsRepository';\n\nexport async function runPointsProjector(): Promise<void> {\n  const consumer = kafka.consumer({\n    groupId: 'gamification-points-projector-v1',\n  });\n\n  await consumer.connect();\n  await consumer.subscribe({\n    topic: topicName('education.assignment'),\n    fromBeginning: false,\n  });\n\n  await consumer.run({\n    eachMessage: async ({ message, partition }) => {\n      try {\n        const raw = message.value?.toString() ?? '{}';\n        const parsed = AssignmentSubmittedEventSchema.parse(JSON.parse(raw));\n\n        await pointsRepo.increment(\n          parsed.payload.studentId,\n          /* points = */ 5,\n        );\n\n        console.info(\n          `[PointProjector] +5 for student=${parsed.payload.studentId} (partition=${partition})`,\n        );\n      } catch (err) {\n        // DLQ or retry logic could be implemented here\n        console.error('[PointProjector] Failed to process message', err);\n      }\n    },\n  });\n}\n```\n\n### 4.5 Snapshotter Utility\n\n```ts\n// src/utils/snapshotter.ts\nimport { kafka, topicName } from '../infrastructure/kafka/kafkaClient';\n\nexport async function publishSnapshot<T>({\n  boundedContext,\n  aggregateName,\n  aggregateId,\n  revision,\n  state,\n}: {\n  boundedContext: string;\n  aggregateName: string;\n  aggregateId: string;\n  revision: number;\n  state: T;\n}): Promise<void> {\n  const producer = kafka.producer();\n\n  await producer.connect();\n  try {\n    await producer.send({\n      topic: topicName(`${boundedContext}.${aggregateName}.snapshot`),\n      messages: [\n        {\n          key  : aggregateId,\n          value: JSON.stringify({\n            schemaVersion: 1,\n            type         : `${aggregateName}.snapshot`,\n            revision,\n            occurredAt   : new Date().toISOString(),\n            state,\n          }),\n        },\n      ],\n    });\n  } finally {\n    await producer.disconnect();\n  }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Migration Path\n\n1. **Brown-field integration**: legacy CRUD modules will emit events in a \u201cchange-data-capture\u201d style, then slowly migrate command handling logic.  \n2. **Feature toggles**: Read models behind `/v2/` API routes will use event projections; `/v1/` remains on relational reads.  \n3. **Runbook & SRE**: New runbooks added for Kafka cluster monitoring (Lag, ISR, Disk usage).  \n4. **Developer enablement**: Internal workshop + \u201cEvent Sourcing 101\u201d wiki page.  \n\n---\n\n## 6. Rejected Alternatives\n\n* **RabbitMQ + Outbox pattern** \u2013 flexible routing but lacks strong log-compaction and replay features.  \n* **Full CQRS without Event Sourcing** \u2013 improves reads but doesn\u2019t solve auditability or temporal requirements.  \n\n---\n\n## 7. Open Issues / Next Steps\n\n1. Define retention policy per topic (regulatory requirement: 5-year minimum).  \n2. Agree on company-wide naming convention for events (`<Domain>.<Action><PastTense>`).  \n3. Evaluate Confluent Schema Registry vs. open-source alternatives.  \n4. Prototype snapshotting performance with 1M-event aggregate.  \n\n---\n\n> \u201cIf you treat data as immutable facts, your systems become a chronicle of truth, not just a reflection of the present.\u201d \u2013  Tech Lead, PCH\n```",

    "content": "```markdown\n# ADR 001 \u2013 Adopt a Polyglot, Event-Driven Microservices Architecture\n\n* Status: **Accepted**  \n* Date: 2024-05-19  \n* Deciders: Architecture Council (CTO, Lead Backend, Lead Frontend, DevOps)  \n* Supersedes: N/A  \n* See also: 002-database-strategy.md, 003-auth-identity.md\n\n---\n\n## 1. Context  \n\nPulseLearn Campus Hub (PL-CH) must enable:\n\n1. Real-time, bidirectional interactions between thousands of concurrent users (students, teachers, admins).  \n2. Rapid feature evolution by autonomous domain-centric teams.  \n3. Fault-tolerance and graceful degradation of non-critical functionality (e.g., delayed \u201cBadgeAwarded\u201d events must **not** block quiz submissions).  \n4. Polyglot technology choices while enforcing a consistent ops/observability contract.  \n5. Compliance with FERPA, GDPR, and internal audit requirements such as end-to-end traceability and PII redaction policies.\n\nThe alternatives considered were:\n\n| Candidate                     | Pros                                                                                                    | Cons                                                                                                   |\n| ----------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |\n| A) Single-service (monolith)  | Simple to deploy, transactional consistency, easier local dev                                           | Scalability bottlenecks, slower team velocity, long-lived branches, risky deployments                  |\n| B) Self-contained services    | Autonomy per bounded context, independent UI + API bundles                                              | Risk of UI duplication, heavier front-end orchestration                                                |\n| **C) Microservices + Event Bus** | Loose coupling via events, horizontal scalability, team autonomy, tech polyglot, easier domain modeling | Requires distributed tracing, eventual consistency semantics, operational complexity                   |\n| D) Serverless (FaaS only)     | Zero infra management, cost per execution                                                               | Cold starts, vendor lock-in, limited long-running connections, complex local testing                   |\n\nAfter evaluating traffic patterns, compliance constraints, and organisation structure (5 cross-functional squads), option **C** was chosen.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Decision  \n\nWe will build **PulseLearn Campus Hub** as an **event-driven microservices system**:\n\n1. **Domain-Oriented Microservices**  \n   \u2022 Each service owns a bounded context & data store (e.g., `UserProfile`, `LearningPath`, `Achievement`, `Notification`).  \n   \u2022 Services communicate asynchronously via a Kafka compatible bus (NATS JetStream in staging, Confluent Cloud in prod).  \n   \u2022 REST/gRPC APIs remain for synchronous \u201cquery\u201d use-cases and external integrations (admin panel, LTI).  \n\n2. **Event Taxonomy**  \n   \u2022 All domain events adopt the CloudEvents 1.0 spec.  \n   \u2022 Topic naming: `pl.<boundedContext>.<eventName>.<version>` (e.g., `pl.achievement.badge_awarded.v1`).  \n   \u2022 Payloads are validated with versioned Avro schemas stored in Schema Registry.  \n\n3. **Shared Platform Libraries**  \n   \u2022 We ship an OSS-friendly **`@pl/platform`** JavaScript package that wraps NATS/Kafka producers & consumers, tracing, and idempotency utilities (see snippet below).  \n   \u2022 Analogous libraries will exist for Python, Go, and Java to keep polyglot parity.  \n\n4. **Observability & Resilience**  \n   \u2022 OpenTelemetry for distributed tracing, correlated logs, metrics (`traceId` + `spanId` pass via W3C `traceparent`).  \n   \u2022 Circuit breakers (opossum) guard cross-service HTTP calls.  \n   \u2022 Retry, DLQ, and \u201cparking lot\u201d patterns for poison messages.  \n\n5. **Security**  \n   \u2022 mTLS between services (Linkerd service mesh).  \n   \u2022 SPIFFE IDs for zero-trust identity.  \n   \u2022 PII encrypted at rest (PostgreSQL + envelope encryption).  \n\n---\n\n## 3. Consequences  \n\nPositive:  \n\u2713 Independent deployability enables <15 min release cadence per squad.  \n\u2713 Horizontal scaling by workload (e.g., `RecommendationService` auto-scales via KEDA based on Kafka lag).  \n\u2713 Failure isolation\u2014`SearchIndexer` crash has no direct impact on \u201cQuizCompletion\u201d UX.  \n\nNegative:  \n\u2717 Added operational overhead: CI/CD pipelines, playbooks, Terraform modules per service.  \n\u2717 Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows like \u201cPurchaseCourse \u2192 ActivateAccess \u2192 EmitInvoice\u201d.  \n\u2717 On-call complexity: PagerDuty rotations per squad, plus a shared SRE roster for platform components (Kafka, Linkerd, Istio ingress).\n\n---\n\n## 4. Implementation Sketch  \n\n### Mermaid: High-level view\n\n```mermaid\nflowchart LR\n    subgraph Frontend\n        ReactApp[Web SPA]\n        MobileApp[React Native]\n    end\n    ReactApp -->|REST: /api/v1| APIGateway\n    MobileApp -->|GraphQL| APIGateway\n    APIGateway --> AuthSvc[(Auth Service)]\n    APIGateway --> UserSvc[(User Profile)]\n    APIGateway --> CourseSvc[(Course Catalog)]\n    style APIGateway fill:#f5f5f5,stroke:#333,stroke-width:1px\n    \n    %% Event Bus\n    subgraph EventBus[\"NATS / Kafka\"]\n        NATS[(JetStream Topic)]\n    end\n    \n    CourseSvc -->|pl.course.uploaded| NATS\n    UserSvc -->|pl.user.session_expired| NATS\n    NATS --> SearchSvc[(Search Indexer)]\n    NATS --> BadgeSvc[(Achievement)]\n    NATS --> RecSvc[(Recommendation)]\n```\n\n### Shared JS Event Library (`@pl/platform`)\n\n```javascript\n// @pl/platform/lib/event-bus.js\nimport { connect, StringCodec } from 'nats';\nimport { v4 as uuid } from 'uuid';\nimport * as otel from '@opentelemetry/api';\n\n/**\n * EventBus singleton to publish/subscribe CloudEvents-compliant messages.\n */\nexport class EventBus {\n  static instance;\n\n  /**\n   * Initialise a NATS connection (lazy).\n   * @param {object} config - {servers: string, jwt?: string, nkey?: string}\n   */\n  static async init(config) {\n    if (!EventBus.instance) {\n      EventBus.instance = new EventBus(config);\n      await EventBus.instance._connect();\n    }\n    return EventBus.instance;\n  }\n\n  constructor(config) {\n    this.config = config;\n    this.sc = StringCodec();\n  }\n\n  async _connect() {\n    try {\n      this.nc = await connect(this.config);\n      this.js = this.nc.jetstream();\n      console.info('[EventBus] Connected to NATS');\n    } catch (err) {\n      console.error('[EventBus] Connection error', err);\n      throw err;\n    }\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Publish a CloudEvent to the given topic.\n   * @param {string} topic - e.g. \"pl.achievement.badge_awarded.v1\"\n   * @param {object} data - event payload\n   * @param {object} [options] - headers, trace context, etc.\n   */\n  async publish(topic, data, options = {}) {\n    if (!this.nc) throw new Error('EventBus not initialised');\n    const span = otel.trace.getTracer('pl-platform').startSpan(`publish:${topic}`);\n    try {\n      const event = {\n        id: uuid(),\n        source: 'pulselearn-campus-hub',\n        specversion: '1.0',\n        type: topic,\n        time: new Date().toISOString(),\n        datacontenttype: 'application/json',\n        data,\n      };\n      // propagate trace context\n      const headers = this._buildHeaders(span, options.headers);\n      await this.js.publish(topic, this.sc.encode(JSON.stringify(event)), { headers });\n      span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.OK });\n    } catch (err) {\n      span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.ERROR, message: err.message });\n      throw err;\n    } finally {\n      span.end();\n    }\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Subscribe to a topic with durable consumer semantics.\n   * @param {string} topic\n   * @param {string} durableName\n   * @param {(evt: object) => Promise<void>} handler\n   */\n  async subscribe(topic, durableName, handler) {\n    const subOpts = { durable: durableName, manualAck: true, ackWait: 60_000 };\n    const sub = await this.js.subscribe(topic, subOpts);\n    console.info(`[EventBus] Subscribed to ${topic}`);\n\n    (async () => {\n      for await (const m of sub) {\n        const span = otel.trace.getTracer('pl-platform').startSpan(`consume:${topic}`);\n        try {\n          const evt = JSON.parse(this.sc.decode(m.data));\n          await handler(evt);\n          m.ack();\n          span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.OK });\n        } catch (err) {\n          console.error('[EventBus] Handler error', err);\n          // let JetStream redeliver, or add to DLQ via a header\n          span.setStatus({ code: otel.SpanStatusCode.ERROR, message: err.message });\n        } finally {\n          span.end();\n        }\n      }\n    })().catch((err) => console.error('[EventBus] Async iteration error', err));\n  }\n\n  _buildHeaders(span, extra = {}) {\n    const headers = this.nc.headers();\n    const ctx = otel.trace.setSpan(otel.context.active(), span);\n    otel.propagation.inject(ctx, headers, {\n      set: (carrier, key, value) => carrier.set(key, value),\n    });\n    Object.entries(extra).forEach(([k, v]) => headers.set(k, v));\n    return headers;\n  }\n}\n```\n\n### Saga Orchestration Example (Enroll Premium Course)\n\n```javascript\n// services/payment/src/enrollCourseSaga.js\nimport { EventBus } from '@pl/platform';\nimport { db } from '../db';\nimport { generateInvoice } from '../billing';\nimport { logger } from '../logger';\n\nexport async function registerEventHandlers() {\n  const bus = await EventBus.init({ servers: process.env.NATS_URL });\n\n  // listen to PaymentCaptured\n  await bus.subscribe('pl.payment.captured.v1', 'enroll-premium-course', async (evt) => {\n    const { userId, courseId, paymentId } = evt.data;\n    logger.info('Payment captured', { userId, courseId, paymentId });\n\n    // Step 1: Activate access in course service (synchronous call)\n    try {\n      await activateCourseAccess(userId, courseId);\n    } catch (err) {\n      logger.error('Course activation failed', err);\n      // emit compensating event\n      await bus.publish('pl.payment.refund_requested.v1', { paymentId, reason: 'COURSE_ACTIVATION_FAILED' });\n      return;\n    }\n\n    // Step 2: Emit EnrollmentGranted event\n    await bus.publish('pl.enrollment.granted.v1', { userId, courseId });\n\n    // Step 3: Issue invoice (local DB + external PDF generator)\n    try {\n      const invoiceId = await generateInvoice({ userId, paymentId });\n      await db.invoice.markSent(invoiceId);\n    } catch (err) {\n      logger.error('Invoice generation failed', err);\n      // Non-blocking; instructor & finance will be alerted via DLQ consumer\n    }\n  });\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## 5. Alternatives Explored (But NOT Chosen)\n\n* **Monolith + Event Module** \u2013 insufficient isolation; high coordination cost for multi-squad development.  \n* **Pure Serverless** \u2013 latency and unpredictable cost for high-frequency message streams (quizzes, edits).  \n* **gRPC-only Service Mesh** \u2013 synchronous coupling failed chaos testing when `AnalyticsService` induced 40 % error rate.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Validation & Next Steps\n\n1. Platform Team to spin up NATS + JetStream in staging (k8s operator).  \n2. Each squad migrates at least one bounded context to the new pattern by Sprint 14.  \n3. Evaluate Confluent vs Redpanda for prod by Q3.  \n4. Conduct load test: 50k concurrent websocket sessions, publish 2k events/s, < 200 ms P99 end-to-end latency.  \n\n---\n\n## 7. References\n\n* \u201cBuilding Event-Driven Microservices\u201d \u2013 O\u2019Reilly, 2021  \n* CloudEvents 1.0 Spec \u2013 https://cloudevents.io/  \n* JetStream Acknowledgements \u2013 https://docs.nats.io/jetstream/consumers/ack_policy  \n* Saga Pattern \u2013 https://microservices.io/patterns/data/saga.html  \n\n```",

*/\nfunction useProgressStream(userId) {\n  const [data, setData] = useState([]);\n  const [loading, setLoading] = useState(Boolean(userId));\n  const [error, setError] = useState(null);\n\n  const ws.addEventListener('open', () => {\n        setLoading(false);\n        setError(null);\n        // Reset reconnect back-off on successful connection\n        reconnectIntervalRef.current = INITIAL_RECONNECT_INTERVAL;\n      });\n\n      ws.addEventListener('message', (msg) => {\n        try {\n          const json = JSON.parse(msg.data);\n\n          /**\n           * Backend sends reconnectIntervalRef.current * 2,\n          MAX_RECONNECT_INTERVAL,\n        );\n\n        setTimeout(connect, timeout);\n      });\n\n      ws.addEventListener('error', (e) => {\n        // We close WS. 'close' listener handles reconnection logic.\n        ws.close();\n        setError('Connection lost. Reconnecting\u2026');\n        // eslint-disable-next-line no-console\n        console.error('Progress WS error', e);\n      });\n    };\n\n    connect();\n\n    // Clean up on component unmount\n    return () => {\n      forcedClose = true;\n      if (wsRef.current && wsRef.current.readyState === WebSocket.OPEN) {\n        wsRef.current.close();\n      }\n    };\n  }, [userId, Built with accessibility, performance, and resiliency in mind.\n */\n\nimport React, {\n  memo,\n  useCallback,\n  useEffect,\n  useRef,\n  useState,\n} from 'react';\nimport PropTypes from                                                                */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\n/**\n * Throttles a function so it is executed at most once every `limit` ms.\n */\nconst throttle = (fn, limit = 200) => {\n  let inThrottle;\n  return (...args) => {\n    if (!inThrottle) {\n      // eslint-disable-next-line prefer-spread\n      fn.apply(null, args);\n      inThrottle = true;\n      setTimeout(() => (inThrottle = false), limit);\n    }\n  };\n};\n\n/**\n * Formats a timestamp into a relative string (e.g., \"3 minutes useState(false);\n  const [error, setError] = useState(null);\n\n  /* --------------------------------- Fetch -------------------------------- */\n\n  /**\n   * Fetches a page of historical activity page: pageNumber,\n            size: PAGE_SIZE,\n            userId,\n          },\n          headers: { Authorization: `Bearer ${token}` },\n          timeout: 10_000,\n        });\n\n        const { ...items.filter((it) => !prev.some((p) => p.id === it.id)),\n          ].sort((a, b) => new Date(b.timestamp) - new Date(a.timestamp)),\n        );\n        setHasMore(!last);\n        setPage(pageNumber);\n      } catch (err) {\n        setError(\n          err.response?.data?.message ||\n            err.message ||\n            'Failed to load activity stream.',\n        );\n Please try again later.');\n      } finally {\n        setLoadingInitial(false);\n        setLoadingMore(false);\n      }\n    },\n    [token, userId],\n  );\n\n  /* ---------------------------- Infinite Scroll --------------------------- */\n\n  const handleScroll = useCallback(\n    throttle(() => {\n      if (!hasMore || loadingMore || !feedRef.current) return;\n\n      const { scrollTop, scrollHeight, clientHeight } = feedRef.current;\n\n      // If scrolled within 100px from bottom, load more\n      if (scrollHeight - scrollTop - clientHeight < 100) {\n        setLoadingMore(true);\n {\n          setActivities((prev) => {\n            const alreadyExists = prev.some((a) => a.id === parsed.event.id);\n            if (alreadyExists) return prev; // ignore duplicates\n            return [parsed.event, ...prev];\n          });\n        }\n      } catch (e) {\n        // eslint-disable-next-line no-console\n        console.warn('Failed to parse websocket message', e);\n      }\n    };\n\n    socket.onerror = (e) => {\n      // eslint-disable-next-line no-console\n      console.error('[ActivityStream] WebSocket error', e);\n      toast.error('Real-time connection lost.');\n    };\n\n    socket.onclose = (e) => {\n      // eslint-disable-next-line no-console\n      console.warn('[ActivityStream] WebSocket closed', e.reason);\n    };\n\n    return () => socket.close(1000, 'Component unmounted');\n  }, [token]);\n\n  /* -------------------------------- Mount --------------------------------- */\n\n  useEffect(() => {\n    fetchPage(0);\n    // eslint-disable-next-line \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n  const handleReady = () => {\n    setReady(true);\n    /* Seek to previous checkpoint (if any) */\n    if (!isNearlyEqual(startAt, 0)) {\n      playerRef.current?.seekTo(startAt, 'seconds');\n    }\n\n    emitEvent('LecturePlayerReady');\n  };\n\n  const handlePlayPause = () => {\n    setPlaying((p) => {\n      const next = !p;\n      emitEvent(next ?  const toggleFullscreen = () => {\n    if (screenfull.isEnabled && containerRef.current) {\n      screenfull.toggle(containerRef.current);\n    }\n  };\n\n  useEffect(() => {\n    if Consumers\n   * receive strongly-typed payloads via an EventEmitter.\n   *\n   * NOTE: This uses native EventSource so that we don\u2019t couple to a\n   * heavy WebSocket lib only for one-way notifications.\n   *\n   * @param {string} courseId\n   * @returns {EventEmitter} emitter \u2013 fires events by their domain type\n   *\n   * Usage:\n   *   const emitter = courseService.subscribe('course_123');\n   *   emitter.on('BadgeAwarded', (evt) => console.log(evt));\n   *   emitter.on('SessionExpired', () => history.push('/login'));\n   *\n   *   // Teardown\n   *   emitter.close();\n   */\n  subscribe(courseId) {\n    const source = new EventSource(\n      `${API_BASE_URL}/realtime/courses/${courseId}`,\n      { withCredentials: true },\n    );\n\n    const emitter = new EventEmitter();\n\n    source.onmessage = (event) => {\n      try {\n        const data = JSON.parse(event.data);\n        // Domain event name expected at data.type\n        emitter.emit(data.type, data.payload);\n      } catch (err) {\n        // Pass raw payload for non-JSON events\n        emitter.emit('message', event.data);\n      }\n    };\n\n    source.onerror = (err) => {\n      emitter.emit('error', err);\n    };\n\n    // Helper to ensure consumer can terminate connection\n    emitter.close = () => {\n      source.close();\n    };\n\n    return emitter;\n  },\n};\n\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n/*                               Named Exports                                */\n/* -------------------------------------------------------------------------- */\n\nexport default courseService;\n```\n",

A typical workflow:\n *\n * 1. Request hits the CourseController                 (MVC)\n * 2. Controller delegates to CourseService             (Service Layer)\n * 3. Service queries DB through Prisma ORM             (Repository Pattern)\n * 4. Service publishes Course domain events to Kafka   (Event Backbone)\n * 5. Service caches hot data in Redis                  (Performance)\n *\n * NOTE: Do not import this file directly from your controllers; always consume\n * it via the service locator (`src/di/index.js`) to keep dependencies swappable\n * and mock-able during tests.\n */\n\n'use strict';\n\n/* \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 Singleton Instances \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 */\nconst prisma  = new PrismaClient();\nconst redis   = new Redis(process.env.REDIS_URL || 'redis://localhost:6379');\n\nconst kafka   = new Kafka({\n  clientId: 'course-service',\n  brokers : (process.env.KAFKA_BROKERS || 'localhost:9092').split(',')\n});\nconst producer = kafka.producer();\n\n/* \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 winston.createLogger({\n  level    : process.env.NODE_ENV === 'production' ? 'info' : 'debug',\n  transports: [\n    new winston.transports.Console({\n      format: winston.format.combine(\n        winston.format.colorize(),\n        winston.format.timestamp(),\n        winston.format.printf(\n          ({ timestamp, level, message, ...meta }) =>\n            `${timestamp} [${level}] ${message} ${Object.keys(meta).length ? Uses Redis with JSON serialization.\n * @param {String} key\n * @param {Function} resolver - Function that returns a Promise of the data\n * @param {Number} ttlSeconds - Time-to-live\n */\nasync function getOrSetCache(key, resolver, ttlSeconds = 60) {\n  const cached = await redis.get(key);\n  if (cached) {\n    return JSON.parse(cached);\n  }\n  const fresh = await resolver();\n  await redis.set(key, JSON.stringify(fresh), 'EX', ttlSeconds);\n  return fresh;\n}\n\n/* \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 Domain Service \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500 */\nclass CourseService {\n  /* ======================================================================= *\n   * PUBLIC API                                                              *\n   * ======================================================================= */\n\n  /**\n   * Creates a brand-new course and its initial metadata.\n   * @param {Object} courseData\n   * @param {String} creatorId\n   * @returns {Promise<Object>} Newly created course\n   */\n  async createCourse(courseData, creatorId) {\n    const { title, description, category, thumbnailUrl, publishedAt } = courseData;\n\n    // Basic validation\n    if (!title || title.length < 3) {\n      throw new AppError('Course title must be at least 3 characters long', ErrorCodes.VALIDATION);\n    }\n\n    try {\n      const course = await prisma.$transaction(async (tx) => {\n        // 1. Insert into Course table\n        const newCourse = await tx.course.create({\n          data: {\n            id          : uuid(),\n            title,\n            description,\n            category,\n            thumbnailUrl,\n            publishedAt : publishedAt || null,\n            creatorId,\n            status      : 'DRAFT'\n          }\n        });\n\n        // 2. Auto-enroll creator as instructor\n        await tx.courseEnrollment.create({\n          data: {\n            userId  : creatorId,\n            courseId: newCourse.id,\n            role    : 'INSTRUCTOR'\n          }\n        });\n\n        return newCourse;\n      });\n\n      // 3. resolve();\n      });\n    });\n  }\n\n  /**\n   * Publish raw subject + message\n   * @param {String} subject\n   * @param {String} message   \u2013 already JSON serialised\n   * @param {Object} @returns {Promise<void>}\n   */\n  async _flushCache() {\n    if (!this.cache) return;\n    const keys = await this.cache.keys('course:*');\n    if (keys.length) await this.cache.del(keys);\n  }\n}\n\nmodule.exports = CourseRepository;\n```",

for generating a robust, battle-tested\n * nginx.conf file that fronts the API-Gateway of the PulseLearn platform.\n *\n * Why JavaScript for an \u201cnginx.conf\u201d?\n * ----------------------------------\n * \u2022 Configuration needs to adapt to dynamic container / k8s deployments.\n * \u2022 Runtime values (hostnames, ports, ssl paths) come from ENV vars.\n * \u2022 We want validation, helpful error messages and unit-testability.\n *\n * Usage\n * -----\n *  $ node nginx.conf [output-path]\n *\n *  \u2013 If executed via `node`, the generated configuration is written to\n *    the provided output path (default: /etc/nginx/conf.d/pulselearn.conf)\n *  \u2013 When imported (`require('./nginx.conf')`) the `buildNginxConfig`\n *    method returns the config as a string.\n */\n\n'use strict';\n\nconst fs   = require('fs');\nconst path = require('path');\nconst os   = require('os');\n\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Environment Schema\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\nconst ENV_SCHEMA = {\n  /** Comma-separated hosts for each micro-service.\n   *  Example: AUTH_SERVICE_HOSTS=\"auth1:4000,auth2:4000\" */\n  AUTH_SERVICE_HOSTS        : { required: true  },\n  USER_SERVICE_HOSTS        : { required: true  },\n  CONTENT_SERVICE_HOSTS     : { required: true  },\n  NOTIFICATION_SERVICE_HOSTS: { required: true  },\n\n  /** SSL certificate / key */\n  SSL_CERT_PATH             : { required: false, default: '/etc/ssl/certs/pulselearn.crt' },\n  SSL_KEY_PATH              : { required: false, default: '/etc/ssl/private/pulselearn.key' },\n\n  /** Optional toggles */\n  FORCE_SSL                 : { required: false, default: 'true' },\n  CLIENT_MAX_BODY_SIZE_MB   : { required: false, default: '20' },\n  RATE_LIMIT_REQ_PER_MIN    : { required: false, default: '600' },\n\n  /** Logging */\n  ACCESS_LOG_PATH           : { required: false, default: '/var/log/nginx/access.log' },\n  ERROR_LOG_PATH            : { required: false, default: '/var/log/nginx/error.log' }\n};\n\n/**\n * Load and validate environment variables against the schema.\n * Throws if a required variable is missing.\n */\nfunction loadEnv () {\n  const conf = {};\n\n  Object.entries(ENV_SCHEMA).forEach(([key, meta]) => {\n    const value = process.env[key] ?? meta.default;\n    if (meta.required && (value === undefined || value === null)) {\n      throw new Error(`Missing required environment variable: ${key}`);\n    }\n    conf[key] = value;\n  });\n\n  return conf;\n}\n\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Helper Functions\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\n/**\n * Parse upstream hosts into nginx `server` directives.\n *\n * @param {string} hostsString - Comma-separated host:port pairs.\n * @returns {string}           - Multi-line string ready to embed.\n */\nfunction toUpstreamServers (hostsString) {\n  return hostsString\n    .split(',')\n    .map(host => host.trim())\n    .filter(Boolean)\n    .map(host => `        server ${host};`)\n    .join('\\n');\n}\n\n/**\n * Render a single upstream block.\n *\n * @param {string} name       - Upstream name (e.g. \"auth_service\").\n * @param {string} hosts      - Comma-separated list of host:port targets.\n * @param {object} [opts={}]  - Options like keepalive settings.\n */\nfunction renderUpstream (name, hosts, opts = {}) {\n  const keepalive = opts.keepalive ?? 64;\n  return `\n    upstream ${name} {\n${toUpstreamServers(hosts)}\n        keepalive ${keepalive};\n    }`;\n}\n\n/**\n * Render a location block that proxies to a given upstream service.\n *\n * @param {string} pathPrefix   - URI prefix (e.g. \"/auth/\").\n * @param {string} upstreamName - Name defined in an `upstream` block.\n */\nfunction renderLocation (pathPrefix, upstreamName) {\n  return `\n            location ${pathPrefix} {\n                proxy_pass          http://${upstreamName};\n                proxy_http_version  1.1;\n                proxy_set_header    Connection \"\";\n                proxy_set_header    Host              $host;\n                proxy_set_header    X-Real-IP         $remote_addr;\n                proxy_set_header    X-Forwarded-For   $proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;\n                proxy_set_header    X-Forwarded-Proto $scheme;\n                proxy_set_header    X-Request-ID      $request_id;\n                proxy_cache_bypass  $cookie_session;\n            }`;\n}\n\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n// Main Config Builder\n////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////////\n\n/**\n * Build the complete nginx.conf string.\n *\n * @returns {string} The final configuration.\n */\nfunction buildNginxConfig () {\n  const env = loadEnv();\n\n  const RATE_LIMIT_ZONE = `\n    limit_req_zone $binary_remote_addr zone=req_limit:${parseInt(env.RATE_LIMIT_REQ_PER_MIN, 10) * 32}k rate=${env.RATE_LIMIT_REQ_PER_MIN}r/m;`;\n\n  const UPSTREAMS = [\n    ['auth_service',          env.AUTH_SERVICE_HOSTS],\n    ['user_service',          env.USER_SERVICE_HOSTS],\n    ['content_service',       env.CONTENT_SERVICE_HOSTS],\n    ['notification_service',  env.NOTIFICATION_SERVICE_HOSTS]\n  ].map(([name, hosts]) => renderUpstream(name, hosts)).join('\\n');\n\n  const LOCATIONS =\n      renderLocation('/auth/',         'auth_service')          +\n      renderLocation('/users/',        'user_service')          +\n      renderLocation('/content/',      'content_service')       +\n      renderLocation('/notifications/','notification_service');\n\n  const SSL_CONFIG = (env.FORCE_SSL === 'true')\n    ? `\n        listen 443 ssl http2;\n        ssl_certificate     ${env.SSL_CERT_PATH};\n        ssl_certificate_key ${env.SSL_KEY_PATH};\n        ssl_protocols       TLSv1.2 TLSv1.3;\n        ssl_ciphers         HIGH:!aNULL:!MD5;\n        ssl_prefer_server_ciphers on;\n        ssl_session_cache   shared:SSL:10m;\n        add_header Strict-Transport-Security \"max-age=31536000; includeSubDomains\" always;`\n    : 'listen 80;';\n\n  const REDIRECT_HTTP_TO_HTTPS = (env.FORCE_SSL === 'true')\n    ? `\n    server {\n        listen      80;\n        server_name _;\n        return 301 https://$host$request_uri;\n    }`\n    : '';\n\n  return `\n###############################################################################\n#  PulseLearn Campus Hub \u2013 Auto-Generated Nginx Configuration\n# `${CONFIG.serviceName}-${uuid()}`,\n  });\n\n  logger.info(`\ud83d\udee9\ufe0f  Connected to NATS`, { servers: CONFIG.nats.servers });\n\n  // Graceful NATS shutdown\n  const cleanup = () => {\n process.on('SIGTERM', cleanup);\n\n  // Subscribe to campus events\n  const sub = nc.subscribe(CONFIG.nats.subscriptionSubject, {\n    queue: CONFIG.nats.durableName,\n  });\n\n  (async () => {\n    for await (const msg of sub) {\n      let data;\n      try {\n        data = jc.decode(msg.data);\n      } catch (_) {\n        data = sc.decode(msg.data);\n      }\n\n      handleDomainEvent(msg.subject, data).catch((err) =>\n        logger.error('Failed handling domain event', { subject: msg.subject, err })\n      );\n    }\n  })().catch((err) => logger.error('NATS subscription error', { err }));\n}\n\nasync function handleDomainEvent(subject, event) {\n  /*\n   * A subject might look like:\n   * campus.assignment.submitted\n   * campus.quiz.completed\n   * campus.badge.awarded\n   */\n  const eventType = subject.replace(/^campus\\./, '');\n  const userId = event.recipientId || event.userId; // Domain payload contract\n  if (!userId) {\n    logger.warn('Event has no userId, ignoring', { subject, event });\n    return;\n  }\n\n  const notification = await notificationRepo.add({\n    userId,\n    eventType,\n    payload: event,\n  });\n\n  // Broadcast via WS\n  io.to(userId).emit('notification', notification);\n  logger.info('\ud83d\udce8  Notification delivered', {\n    userId,\n    notificationId: notification.id,\n  });\n}\n\n/* \u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\u2500\n * Bootstrap\n * */\n\nasync function start() {\n  try {\n    await ensureSchema();\n    await bootstrapNats();\n\n    httpServer.listen(CONFIG.port, () => {\n      logger.info(`\ud83d\ude80  ${CONFIG.serviceName} running`, { port: CONFIG.port });\n    });\n\n    // Graceful HTTP shutdown\n    const shutdown = () => {\n      logger.info('Shutting down HTTP server\u2026');\n      httpServer.close(() => {\n        logger.info('HTTP server closed');\n        db.end(() => {\n          logger.info('DB pool closed');\n          process.exit(0);\n        });\n      });\n    };\n    process.on('SIGINT', shutdown);\n    process.on('SIGTERM', shutdown);\n  } catch (err) {\n    logger.error('Failed to bootstrap service', { err });\n    process.exit(1);\n  }\n}\n\nstart();\n```",

    "content": "<!--\n  ADR 003: Polyglot Persistence\n  PulseLearn Campus Hub\n  Status: Accepted\n  Date: 2024-05-28\n-->\n\n# 003 \u2013 Polyglot Persistence  \n\n## Status  \nAccepted \u2013 The decision has been implemented in `v1.4.0`.\n\n## Context  \nPulseLearn Campus Hub is an event-driven system with a variety of read/write patterns:\n\n* Write-intensive, append-only domain events (\u22488 k eps peak)  \n* Read-heavy social timelines that must fan-out to thousands of users in < 150 ms  \n* Strongly-consistent, relational data for billing, LMS compliance, and audit logs  \n* Full-text search over course content and peer-review comments  \n* Graph-style traversals for cohort relationships and content recommendations\n\nA single storage engine cannot optimize for all these needs without unacceptable trade-offs in performance, cost, or developer productivity. We therefore evaluated several strategies:\n\n| Option | Pros | Cons |\n| ------ | ---- | ---- |\n| 1. Single SQL RDBMS (PostgreSQL) | ACID, mature tooling | Hot partitions, expensive scaling, poor search |\n| 2. Single document DB (MongoDB) | Flexible schema, good read scaling | Event ordering issues, multi-doc transactions slower |\n| 3. Polyglot persistence *(selected)* | Fit-for-purpose stores, cost-effective | Operational complexity, cross-store transactions |\n\n## Decision  \nWe adopt **polyglot persistence**: each bounded context chooses the persistence technology that best serves its needs, within guardrails enforced by the Platform Team.\n\n1. **Event Store**  \n   *Technology:* Apache Kafka (log), TimescaleDB (cold storage)  \n   *Rationale:* Immutability, temporal queries, built-in replication.\n\n2. **User & Billing**  \n   *Technology:* PostgreSQL 15 with logical replication  \n   *Rationale:* Strong consistency for payments, GDPR data-subject requests.\n\n3. **Realtime Timelines & Notifications**  \n   *Technology:* Redis Cluster + Redis Streams  \n   *Rationale:* Sub-millisecond fan-out, pub/sub semantics, TTL-based eviction.\n\n4. **Search & Analytics**  \n   *Technology:* OpenSearch 2.x  \n   *Rationale:* Relevance scoring, aggregations, horizontal scaling.\n\n5. **Graph Recommendations**  \n   *Technology:* Neo4j 5.x  \n   *Rationale:* Native graph traversals for \u201cstudents who liked X also liked Y\u201d.\n\n6. **File Storage (Assignments, Media)**  \n   *Technology:* S3-compatible object store with signed URLs  \n   *Rationale:* Durable, CDN-friendly, off-loads traffic from app servers.\n\n### Access Pattern Enforcement  \n```mermaid\ngraph TD\n  subgraph Service Layer\n    SVC[Micro-service]\n  end\n  subgraph Repositories\n    REPO1[(PostgreSQL Repo)]\n    REPO2[(Redis Repo)]\n    REPO3[(Kafka Repo)]\n  end\n  SVC --> REPO1 & REPO2 & REPO3\n```\n\nRepositories shield business logic from vendor SDKs. All repositories implement:\n\n```ts\n// docs/examples/Repository.ts\nexport interface Repository<T> {\n  findById(id: string): Promise<T | null>;\n  save(entity: T): Promise<void>;\n  delete(id: string): Promise<void>;\n}\n```\n\nConcrete adapters (e.g., `UserPgRepository`, `TimelineRedisRepository`) live in their respective packages.\n\n### Data-Contracts & Async Sync  \nCross-store ownership is disallowed; instead we replicate immutable projections using Kafka topics suffixed with `.projection`. Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency while avoiding distributed transactions.\n\n## Consequences  \nPositive\n* Services scale independently; no single datastore becomes a bottleneck.\n* Teams can evolve schemas without cross-team migration battles.\n* Disaster recovery is narrowed to datastore-specific SLAs.\n\nNegative\n* Ops: multiple backup/restore, monitoring, and upgrade procedures.\n* Observability: needing distributed tracing across store boundaries.\n* Onboarding: developers must learn \u2265 3 query DSLs.\n\nMitigations\n* Unified secrets via Vault; IaC modules standardize provisioning.\n* Cross-store dashboards in Grafana/Loki/Tempo.\n* Internal workshops and cheat-sheets for new engineers.\n\n## Related Decisions  \n* ADR-001 \u2013 Event-Driven Architecture  \n* ADR-002 \u2013 Domain-Driven Repository Pattern\n\n## Notes  \nThis ADR will be revisited after the next academic year or when datastore OPEX exceeds 20 % of infrastructure budget.",

  },
