  "content": "# Architectural Analysis Report: User Progress Update Latency in PulseLearn Campus Hub\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThis report provides a root cause analysis of the intermittent latency (up to 60 seconds) users experience when their progress updates are reflected on the dashboard after completing course lectures or quizzes. After tracing the complete end-to-end data flow through the microservices architecture, I have identified that the primary cause is the **inherent eventual consistency** of the event-driven architecture, compounded by specific infrastructure and design choices that amplify latency under load.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Complete End-to-End Data Flow Trace\n\nThe user progress update flow involves two distinct pathways: a **synchronous write path** and an **asynchronous read path** with event propagation in between.\n\n### 1.1 Synchronous Write Path (User Action to Database Persistence)\n\n```\n[User completes lecture]\n    \u2192 [LecturePlayer.js]\n    \u2192 [HTTP PUT/POST to API Gateway]\n    \u2192 [NGINX reverse proxy]\n    \u2192 [course-service Controller]\n    \u2192 [courseService.js]\n    \u2192 [PostgreSQL via Prisma]\n    \u2192 [Kafka/NATS Event Published]\n```\n\n**Detailed Flow:**\n\n1. **Frontend Trigger** (`frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js:181-189`):\n   - When video playback ends, `handleEnded()` is called\n   - Emits a `LectureCompleted` event via the client-side eventBus\n   - Makes a synchronous POST to `/courses/${courseId}/lectures/${lectureId}/complete`\n   - Also saves progress periodically via throttled PUT to `/courses/${courseId}/lectures/${lectureId}/progress` (every 5 seconds)\n\n2. **API Gateway Routing** (`services/api-gateway/nginx.conf`):\n   - NGINX proxies requests to upstream `content_service`\n   - Rate limiting configured at 600 requests/minute per IP\n   - Standard HTTP/1.1 proxying with keepalive connections (64 max)\n\n3. **Course Service Processing** (`services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:317-350`):\n   - `completeLesson()` method handles the completion\n   - Uses Redis-based idempotency lock (`NX`, 5-second TTL) to prevent duplicate processing\n   - Persists completion to PostgreSQL via Prisma (`lessonCompletion` table)\n   - Publishes `LESSON_COMPLETED` event to Kafka via `publishEvent()`\n\n4. **Event Publishing** (`services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:72-93`):\n   - Producer connects to Kafka brokers (lazy connect)\n   - Message includes trace-id header for observability\n   - Non-blocking: errors are logged but not thrown (fire-and-forget pattern)\n\n### 1.2 Asynchronous Event Propagation Path\n\n```\n[Kafka Topic: LESSON_COMPLETED]\n    \u2192 [notification-service consumer]\n    \u2192 [PostgreSQL (notifications table)]\n    \u2192 [Socket.IO broadcast to user room]\n```\n\n**Detailed Flow:**\n\n1. **Event Consumption** (`services/notification-service/src/server.js:303-322`):\n   - NATS subscription with queue group `notification-service-durable`\n   - Subscribes to wildcard subject `campus.>` to receive all domain events\n   - Decodes JSON/String payloads and routes to `handleDomainEvent()`\n\n2. **Notification Persistence & Broadcast** (`server.js:324-350`):\n   - Extracts `userId` from event payload\n   - Persists notification to PostgreSQL\n   - Broadcasts via Socket.IO to user's private room (`io.to(userId).emit('notification', ...)`)\n\n### 1.3 Frontend Read Path (Dashboard Data Retrieval)\n\n```\n[Dashboard loads]\n    \u2192 [DashboardService.getSnapshot()]\n    \u2192 [HTTP GET /dashboard]\n    \u2192 [API Gateway]\n    \u2192 [Backend aggregation]\n    \u2192 [Response to React state]\n\n[WebSocket connection]\n    \u2192 [Socket.IO: dashboard-event]\n    \u2192 [React state update]\n```\n\n**Detailed Flow:**\n\n1. **Initial Dashboard Load** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:139-156`):\n   - `fetchDashboardSnapshot()` makes REST call to `/dashboard` endpoint\n   - Receives metrics, activity feed, and progress chart data\n   - Data reflects the state at the moment of query\n\n2. **Real-time Updates via WebSocket** (`DashboardPage.js:182-223`):\n   - Socket.IO connection to `REACT_APP_WS_ENDPOINT`\n   - Listens for `dashboard-event` messages\n   - Handles `ProgressUpdated` event type to update chart data\n   - Handles `FeedItem` for activity stream updates\n\n3. **ProgressChart WebSocket** (`frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:62-174`):\n   - Separate WebSocket to `wss://api.pulselearn.com/ws/progress/${userId}`\n   - Receives snapshot or granular progress events\n   - Maps events to chart data format\n\n4. **ActivityStream Polling + WebSocket** (`frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js:85-208`):\n   - Initial REST fetch from `/api/v1/activity-stream` with pagination\n   - Concurrent WebSocket subscription for real-time event push\n   - De-duplicates by event ID\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Architectural Components Involved\n\n### 2.1 Services\n\n| Service | Role | Key Files |\n|---------|------|-----------|\n| **API Gateway** | Request routing, rate limiting, SSL termination | `services/api-gateway/nginx.conf`, `docker-compose.yml:206-224` |\n| **course-service** | Course CRUD, progress tracking, event publishing | `src/services/courseService.js`, `src/api/courseController.js`, `src/events/producer.js` |\n| **notification-service** | Event consumption, notification persistence, WebSocket push | `src/server.js` |\n| **activity-service** | Activity feed aggregation | Referenced in `docker-compose.yml:235-244` |\n\n### 2.2 Infrastructure\n\n| Component | Purpose | Configuration Reference |\n|-----------|---------|------------------------|\n| **Kafka (Confluent 7.5.0)** | Event backbone, at-least-once delivery | `docker-compose.yml:120-140`, single broker |\n| **NATS (2.10)** | Alternative message broker with JetStream | `docker-compose.yml:141-152` |\n| **PostgreSQL (15-alpine)** | Relational persistence | `docker-compose.yml:75-91` |\n| **Redis (7-alpine)** | Caching, session store, pub/sub | `docker-compose.yml:92-105` |\n| **NGINX (1.25)** | Reverse proxy | `docker-compose.yml:294-316` |\n\n### 2.3 Critical Code Modules\n\n| Module | Purpose | Location |\n|--------|---------|----------|\n| `courseService.completeLesson()` | Handles lesson completion, publishes event | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:317-350` |\n| `publishEvent()` | Kafka producer abstraction | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:72-93` |\n| `EventProducer` | NATS Streaming producer | `services/course-service/src/events/producer.js` |\n| `handleDomainEvent()` | Event handler in notification service | `services/notification-service/src/server.js:324-350` |\n| `DashboardService.getSnapshot()` | REST API for dashboard data | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:339-365` |\n| `useProgressStream()` | WebSocket hook for real-time progress | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:62-174` |\n\n### 2.4 Database Schemas\n\n| Schema | Purpose | Reference |\n|--------|---------|-----------|\n| `course_service.Enrollment` | Tracks progress (0-100%) | `services/course-service/src/models/schema.prisma:127-141` |\n| `course_service.EventOutbox` | Transactional outbox pattern | `schema.prisma:225-235` |\n| `notifications` | User notifications | `notification-service/src/server.js:100-113` |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Top 3 Most Likely Architectural Bottlenecks\n\n### Bottleneck #1: Single Kafka Broker with No Partitioning (HIGHEST PROBABILITY)\n\n**Evidence:**\n\nFrom `docker-compose.yml:120-140`:\n```yaml\nkafka:\n  image: confluentinc/cp-kafka:7.5.0\n  environment:\n    KAFKA_BROKER_ID: 1\n    KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\n\n1. **Single Broker Configuration**: The `KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1` and `KAFKA_BROKER_ID: 1` indicate a single-broker deployment. This creates a bottleneck because:\n   - All producers contend for the same broker\n   - No parallel partition processing for consumers\n   - Under peak load, producer ACKs queue up\n\n2. **Lazy Producer Connection** (`services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:74-75`):\n   ```javascript\n   await producer.connect(); // NOOP after first call\n   await producer.send({...});\n   ```\n   While the connect is cached, each `send()` blocks until ACK is received. With a single broker under load, this introduces latency.\n\n3. **Fire-and-Forget Error Handling** (`courseService.js:91`):\n   ```javascript\n   } catch (err) {\n     // We never throw from publishEvent; instead we log and continue.\n     logger.error('Failed to publish event', { topic, err: err.stack || err });\n   }\n   ```\n   This means transient Kafka failures result in lost events, which would cause dashboard updates to never arrive.\n\n**Architectural Justification:**\n- ADR-002 (`docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md:43-49`) specifies using Kafka as the persistent event store\n- The ADR acknowledges trade-offs: \"Consumers can restart and replay without data loss\"\n- However, the single-broker config doesn't align with the stated \"horizontal partitioning of event streams\" goal\n\n**Impact Under Load:**\n- At peak (8k events/sec per ADR-003), a single broker cannot maintain sub-200ms latency\n- Consumer lag accumulates, causing the intermittent 30-60 second delays users report\n\n---\n\n### Bottleneck #2: Eventual Consistency and Cache Invalidation Lag\n\n**Evidence:**\n\nFrom `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:101-109`:\n```javascript\nasync function getOrSetCache(key, resolver, ttlSeconds = 60) {\n  const cached = await redis.get(key);\n  if (cached) {\n    return JSON.parse(cached);\n  }\n  const fresh = await resolver();\n  await redis.set(key, JSON.stringify(fresh), 'EX', ttlSeconds);\n  return fresh;\n}\n```\n\nAnd cache invalidation on write (`courseService.js:342`):\n```javascript\nawait redis.del(`course:${courseId}:*`);\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\n\n1. **60-Second Cache TTL**: Course data is cached for 60 seconds. When the dashboard fetches progress, it may receive stale data if:\n   - The cache was populated before the lesson completion\n   - The cache key pattern for invalidation (`course:*`) may not cover all read variations\n\n2. **Event \u2192 Cache Invalidation Timing**: The flow is:\n   - User completes lesson \u2192 DB write \u2192 Cache invalidated \u2192 Event published\n   - Event consumed \u2192 Notification created \u2192 WebSocket push\n\n   If the WebSocket push fails or the user's WebSocket disconnects briefly, they fall back to REST polling. The next REST call may still hit the cached (stale) data if TTL hasn't expired.\n\n3. **Progress Percentage Not Real-Time** (`schema.prisma:132`):\n   ```prisma\n   progress   Decimal          @db.Decimal(5, 2) // percentage 0.00-100.00\n   ```\n   This progress field on `Enrollment` requires re-aggregation when a lesson is completed. This aggregation may be handled by a separate projection consumer that has its own lag.\n\n**Architectural Justification:**\n- ADR-003 (`docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md:83-85`) explicitly states: \"Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing **eventual consistency** while avoiding distributed transactions.\"\n- This is a documented trade-off, but the 60-second delay reported by users suggests the eventual consistency window is too large for user expectations.\n\n---\n\n### Bottleneck #3: Frontend WebSocket Connection Reliability and Fallback Behavior\n\n**Evidence:**\n\nFrom `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:96-174`:\n```javascript\nconst connect = () => {\n  const wsUrl = `wss://api.pulselearn.com/ws/progress/${encodeURIComponent(userId)}`;\n  const ws = new WebSocket(wsUrl);\n  //...\n  ws.addEventListener('close', () => {\n    if (forcedClose) return;\n    setLoading(true);\n    const timeout = reconnectIntervalRef.current;\n    reconnectIntervalRef.current = Math.min(\n      reconnectIntervalRef.current * 2,\n      MAX_RECONNECT_INTERVAL,  // 30 seconds\n    );\n    setTimeout(connect, timeout);\n  });\n};\n```\n\nAnd from `DashboardPage.js:240-252`:\n```javascript\nuseEffect(() => {\n  if (!token) {\n    navigate('/login');\n    return undefined;\n  }\n  fetchDashboardSnapshot();  // Single REST call on mount\n  initSocket();\n  return () => cleanupResources();\n}, [token, fetchDashboardSnapshot, initSocket, navigate]);\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\n\n1. **No Periodic Polling Fallback**: The dashboard makes a single REST call on mount (`fetchDashboardSnapshot()`) and then relies entirely on WebSocket for updates. If:\n   - The WebSocket connection drops\n   - The reconnect is in progress (exponential backoff up to 30 seconds)\n   - The server-side event was emitted during the disconnection window\n\n   ...the user will not see updates until they manually refresh or the WebSocket reconnects.\n\n2. **Multiple Disconnected WebSocket Streams**: The architecture has:\n   - `DashboardPage.js` Socket.IO connection for `dashboard-event`\n   - `ProgressChart.js` native WebSocket to `/ws/progress/${userId}`\n   - `ActivityStream.js` WebSocket to `/ws/activity`\n\n   Each has independent reconnection logic. If any one fails, that specific UI component shows stale data.\n\n3. **No Heartbeat/Health Check**: The WebSocket connections don't implement application-level heartbeats. TCP keepalives may not detect \"zombie\" connections where the server believes the client is connected but messages aren't flowing.\n\n**Architectural Justification:**\n- The component comments acknowledge the design: \"Falls back to placeholder if no WS yet\" (`ProgressChart.js:197`)\n- However, the fallback is just cached static data, not periodic re-fetching\n- ADR-001 states \"fault-tolerance and graceful degradation\" but the frontend implementation assumes happy-path WebSocket connectivity\n\n---\n\n## 4. Synthesis: Why the Delay is \"Intermittent\" and \"Worse Under Load\"\n\nThe reported symptoms\u2014**intermittent delays** that **worsen during peak hours**\u2014are classic indicators of an event-driven architecture under contention:\n\n1. **Kafka Consumer Lag Accumulation**: When message production rate exceeds consumption rate, lag grows. The notification-service queue group processes messages sequentially, so high-volume periods cause backlog.\n\n2. **Cache Serving Stale Data During High Load**: When many users are active:\n   - Cache hit rates increase (good for performance, bad for freshness)\n   - Invalidation patterns may miss edge cases\n   - New reads may hit recently-stale cache entries\n\n3. **WebSocket Infrastructure Bottlenecks**: Socket.IO server in notification-service handles all connected users. Under load:\n   - Room broadcasts (`io.to(userId).emit()`) may queue\n   - Memory pressure on the single service instance\n   - Docker network latency compounds\n\n4. **No End-to-End Backpressure**: The fire-and-forget event publishing means producers don't slow down when consumers are lagging. This allows the problem to compound.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Understanding of Architectural Trade-offs\n\nThis latency is **fundamentally a trade-off of the chosen loosely-coupled, event-driven architecture**. As documented in:\n\n- **ADR-001** (`001-microservices-architecture.md:72-75`): \"Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows\"\n- **ADR-002** (`002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md:65-68`): \"Learning curve \u2013 developers must understand eventual consistency\"\n- **ADR-003** (`003-polyglot-persistence.md:83-85`): \"Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency\"\n\nThe architecture **correctly prioritizes**:\n- Service autonomy and independent deployability\n- Fault isolation (course-service crash doesn't affect dashboard reads)\n- Horizontal scalability (add more consumers to reduce lag)\n\nThe architecture **trades away**:\n- Strong consistency guarantees\n- Instantaneous UI updates\n- Simplicity of data flow tracing\n\n**The 30-60 second delay is not a bug but an emergent property of the architectural choices under specific load conditions.** The system works \"correctly\"\u2014events are delivered eventually\u2014but user expectations for sub-second updates conflict with the eventual consistency model.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Summary of Findings\n\n| Bottleneck | Root Cause | Supporting Evidence |\n|------------|------------|---------------------|\n| **#1 Kafka Throughput** | Single broker, no partitioning | `docker-compose.yml:120-140`, `courseService.js:72-93` |\n| **#2 Cache Staleness** | 60s TTL, async invalidation | `courseService.js:101-109`, ADR-003 |\n| **#3 WebSocket Reliability** | No polling fallback, independent reconnection | `ProgressChart.js:139-151`, `DashboardPage.js:240-252` |\n\nThe combination of these factors explains why:\n- **Delays are intermittent**: Only occur when Kafka lag or cache staleness aligns with user action\n- **Worse under peak load**: Consumer lag grows non-linearly with event volume\n- **Up to 60 seconds**: Matches the cache TTL and max WebSocket reconnect interval\n\n---\n\n## 7. Appendix: File Reference Index\n\n| File | Path | Purpose |\n|------|------|---------|\n| Architecture Overview | `docs/architecture.md` | System design documentation |\n| ADR-001 | `docs/ADR/001-microservices-architecture.md` | Microservices decision |\n| ADR-002 | `docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md` | Event sourcing decision |\n| ADR-003 | `docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md` | Polyglot persistence decision |\n| Docker Compose | `docker-compose.yml` | Infrastructure configuration |\n| NGINX Config Builder | `services/api-gateway/nginx.conf` | API Gateway routing |\n| Course Service | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js` | Core business logic |\n| Course Controller | `services/course-service/src/api/courseController.js` | REST endpoints |\n| Event Producer | `services/course-service/src/events/producer.js` | NATS event publishing |\n| Course Repository | `services/course-service/src/repositories/courseRepository.js` | Data access |\n| Prisma Schema | `services/course-service/src/models/schema.prisma` | Database models |\n| Notification Service | `services/notification-service/src/server.js` | Event consumer + WebSocket |\n| Dashboard Page | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` | Main dashboard component |\n| Progress Chart | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` | Real-time progress viz |\n| Activity Stream | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js` | Activity feed component |\n| Lecture Player | `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` | Video player + progress tracking |\n| Course Service (FE) | `frontend/src/services/courseService.js` | Frontend API client |\n",
  "file_path": "/logs/agent/solution.md"

Rate limiting configured at 600 requests/minute per IP\n   - Standard HTTP/1.1 proxying with keepalive connections (64 max)\n\n3. **Course Service Processing** (`services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:317-350`):\n   - `completeLesson()` method handles the completion\n   - Uses Redis-based idempotency lock (`NX`, 5-second TTL) to prevent duplicate processing\n   - Persists completion to PostgreSQL via Prisma (`lessonCompletion` table)\n   - Publishes `LESSON_COMPLETED` event to Kafka via `publishEvent()`\n\n4. **Event Publishing** (`services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:72-93`):\n   - Producer connects to Kafka brokers (lazy connect)\n   - Message includes trace-id header for observability\n   - Non-blocking: errors are logged but not thrown (fire-and-forget pattern)\n\n### 1.2 Asynchronous Event Propagation Path\n\n```\n[Kafka Topic: LESSON_COMPLETED]\n    \u2192 [notification-service consumer]\n    \u2192 [PostgreSQL (notifications table)]\n    \u2192 [Socket.IO broadcast to user room]\n```\n\n**Detailed Flow:**\n\n1. **Event Consumption** (`services/notification-service/src/server.js:303-322`):\n   - NATS subscription with queue group `notification-service-durable`\n   - Subscribes to wildcard subject `campus.>` to receive all domain events\n   - Decodes JSON/String payloads and routes to `handleDomainEvent()`\n\n2. **Notification Persistence & Broadcast** (`server.js:324-350`):\n   - Extracts `userId` from event payload\n   - Persists notification to PostgreSQL\n   - Broadcasts via Socket.IO to user's private room (`io.to(userId).emit('notification', ...)`)\n\n### 1.3 Frontend Read Path (Dashboard Data Retrieval)\n\n```\n[Dashboard loads]\n    \u2192 [DashboardService.getSnapshot()]\n    \u2192 [HTTP GET /dashboard]\n    \u2192 [API Gateway]\n    \u2192 [Backend aggregation]\n    \u2192 [Response to React state]\n\n[WebSocket connection]\n    \u2192 [Socket.IO: dashboard-event]\n    \u2192 [React state update]\n```\n\n**Detailed Flow:**\n\n1. **Initial Dashboard Load** (`frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:139-156`):\n   - `fetchDashboardSnapshot()` makes REST call to `/dashboard` endpoint\n   - Receives metrics, activity feed, and progress chart data\n   - Data reflects the state at the moment of query\n\n2. **Real-time Updates via WebSocket** (`DashboardPage.js:182-223`):\n   - Socket.IO connection to `REACT_APP_WS_ENDPOINT`\n   - Listens for `dashboard-event` messages\n   - Handles `ProgressUpdated` event type to update chart data\n   - Handles `FeedItem` for activity stream updates\n\n3. **ProgressChart WebSocket** (`frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:62-174`):\n   - Separate WebSocket to `wss://api.pulselearn.com/ws/progress/${userId}`\n   - Receives snapshot or granular progress events\n   - Maps events to chart data format\n\n4. **ActivityStream Polling + WebSocket** (`frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js:85-208`):\n   - Initial REST fetch from `/api/v1/activity-stream` with pagination\n   - Concurrent WebSocket subscription for real-time event push\n   - De-duplicates by event ID\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Architectural Components Involved\n\n### 2.1 Services\n\n| Service | Role | Key Files |\n|---------|------|-----------|\n| **API Gateway** | Request routing, rate limiting, SSL termination | `services/api-gateway/nginx.conf`, `docker-compose.yml:206-224` |\n| **course-service** | Course CRUD, progress tracking, event publishing | `src/services/courseService.js`, `src/api/courseController.js`, `src/events/producer.js` |\n| **notification-service** | Event consumption, notification persistence, WebSocket push | `src/server.js` |\n| **activity-service** | Activity feed aggregation | Referenced in `docker-compose.yml:235-244` |\n\n### 2.2 Infrastructure\n\n| Component | Purpose | Configuration Reference |\n|-----------|---------|------------------------|\n| **Kafka (Confluent 7.5.0)** | Event backbone, at-least-once delivery | `docker-compose.yml:120-140`, single broker |\n| **NATS (2.10)** | Alternative message broker with JetStream | `docker-compose.yml:141-152` |\n| **PostgreSQL (15-alpine)** | Relational persistence | `docker-compose.yml:75-91` |\n| **Redis (7-alpine)** | Caching, session store, pub/sub | `docker-compose.yml:92-105` |\n| **NGINX (1.25)** | Reverse proxy | `docker-compose.yml:294-316` |\n\n### 2.3 Critical Code Modules\n\n| Module | Purpose | Location |\n|--------|---------|----------|\n| `courseService.completeLesson()` | Handles lesson completion, publishes event | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:317-350` |\n| `publishEvent()` | Kafka producer abstraction | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:72-93` |\n| `EventProducer` | NATS Streaming producer | `services/course-service/src/events/producer.js` |\n| `handleDomainEvent()` | Event handler in notification service | `services/notification-service/src/server.js:324-350` |\n| `DashboardService.getSnapshot()` | REST API for dashboard data | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js:339-365` |\n| `useProgressStream()` | WebSocket hook for real-time progress | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:62-174` |\n\n### 2.4 Database Schemas\n\n| Schema | Purpose | Reference |\n|--------|---------|-----------|\n| `course_service.Enrollment` | Tracks progress (0-100%) | `services/course-service/src/models/schema.prisma:127-141` |\n| `course_service.EventOutbox` | Transactional outbox pattern | `schema.prisma:225-235` |\n| `notifications` | User notifications | `notification-service/src/server.js:100-113` |\n\n---\n\n## 3. Top 3 Most Likely Architectural Bottlenecks\n\n### Bottleneck #1: Single Kafka Broker with No Partitioning (HIGHEST PROBABILITY)\n\n**Evidence:**\n\nFrom `docker-compose.yml:120-140`:\n```yaml\nkafka:\n  image: confluentinc/cp-kafka:7.5.0\n  environment:\n    KAFKA_BROKER_ID: 1\n    KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\n\n1. **Single Broker Configuration**: The `KAFKA_OFFSETS_TOPIC_REPLICATION_FACTOR: 1` and `KAFKA_BROKER_ID: 1` indicate a single-broker deployment. This creates a bottleneck because:\n   - All producers contend for the same broker\n   - No parallel partition processing for consumers\n   - Under peak load, producer ACKs queue up\n\n2. **Lazy Producer Connection** (`services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:74-75`):\n   ```javascript\n   await producer.connect(); // NOOP after first call\n   await producer.send({...});\n   ```\n   While the connect is cached, each `send()` blocks until ACK is received. With a single broker under load, this introduces latency.\n\n3. **Fire-and-Forget Error Handling** (`courseService.js:91`):\n   ```javascript\n   } catch (err) {\n     // We never throw from publishEvent; instead we log and continue.\n     logger.error('Failed to publish event', { topic, err: err.stack || err });\n   }\n   ```\n   This means transient Kafka failures result in lost events, which would cause dashboard updates to never arrive.\n\n**Architectural Justification:**\n- ADR-002 (`docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md:43-49`) specifies using Kafka as the persistent event store\n- The ADR acknowledges trade-offs: \"Consumers can restart and replay without data loss\"\n- However, the single-broker config doesn't align with the stated \"horizontal partitioning of event streams\" goal\n\n**Impact Under Load:**\n- At peak (8k events/sec per ADR-003), a single broker cannot maintain sub-200ms latency\n- Consumer lag accumulates, causing the intermittent 30-60 second delays users report\n\n---\n\n### Bottleneck #2: Eventual Consistency and Cache Invalidation Lag\n\n**Evidence:**\n\nFrom `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js:101-109`:\n```javascript\nasync function getOrSetCache(key, resolver, ttlSeconds = 60) {\n  const cached = await redis.get(key);\n  if (cached) {\n    return JSON.parse(cached);\n  }\n  const fresh = await resolver();\n  await redis.set(key, JSON.stringify(fresh), 'EX', ttlSeconds);\n  return fresh;\n}\n```\n\nAnd cache invalidation on write (`courseService.js:342`):\n```javascript\nawait redis.del(`course:${courseId}:*`);\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\n\n1. **60-Second Cache TTL**: Course data is cached for 60 seconds. When the dashboard fetches progress, it may receive stale data if:\n   - The cache was populated before the lesson completion\n   - The cache key pattern for invalidation (`course:*`) may not cover all read variations\n\n2. **Event \u2192 Cache Invalidation Timing**: The flow is:\n   - User completes lesson \u2192 DB write \u2192 Cache invalidated \u2192 Event published\n   - Event consumed \u2192 Notification created \u2192 WebSocket push\n\n   If the WebSocket push fails or the user's WebSocket disconnects briefly, they fall back to REST polling. The next REST call may still hit the cached (stale) data if TTL hasn't expired.\n\n3. **Progress Percentage Not Real-Time** (`schema.prisma:132`):\n   ```prisma\n   progress   Decimal          @db.Decimal(5, 2) // percentage 0.00-100.00\n   ```\n   This progress field on `Enrollment` requires re-aggregation when a lesson is completed. This aggregation may be handled by a separate projection consumer that has its own lag.\n\n**Architectural Justification:**\n- ADR-003 (`docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md:83-85`) explicitly states: \"Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing **eventual consistency** while avoiding distributed transactions.\"\n- This is a documented trade-off, but the 60-second delay reported by users suggests the eventual consistency window is too large for user expectations.\n\n---\n\n### Bottleneck #3: Frontend WebSocket Connection Reliability and Fallback Behavior\n\n**Evidence:**\n\nFrom `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js:96-174`:\n```javascript\nconst connect = () => {\n  const wsUrl = `wss://api.pulselearn.com/ws/progress/${encodeURIComponent(userId)}`;\n  const ws = new WebSocket(wsUrl);\n  //...\n  ws.addEventListener('close', () => {\n    if (forcedClose) return;\n    setLoading(true);\n    const timeout = reconnectIntervalRef.current;\n    reconnectIntervalRef.current = Math.min(\n      reconnectIntervalRef.current * 2,\n      MAX_RECONNECT_INTERVAL,  // 30 seconds\n    );\n    setTimeout(connect, timeout);\n  });\n};\n```\n\nAnd from `DashboardPage.js:240-252`:\n```javascript\nuseEffect(() => {\n  if (!token) {\n    navigate('/login');\n    return undefined;\n  }\n  fetchDashboardSnapshot();  // Single REST call on mount\n  initSocket();\n  return () => cleanupResources();\n}, [token, fetchDashboardSnapshot, initSocket, navigate]);\n```\n\n**Analysis:**\n\n1. **No Periodic Polling Fallback**: The dashboard makes a single REST call on mount (`fetchDashboardSnapshot()`) and then relies entirely on WebSocket for updates. If:\n   - The WebSocket connection drops\n   - The reconnect is in progress (exponential backoff up to 30 seconds)\n   - The server-side event was emitted during the disconnection window\n\n   ...the user will not see updates until they manually refresh or the WebSocket reconnects.\n\n2. **Multiple Disconnected WebSocket Streams**: The architecture has:\n   - `DashboardPage.js` Socket.IO connection for `dashboard-event`\n   - `ProgressChart.js` native WebSocket to `/ws/progress/${userId}`\n   - `ActivityStream.js` WebSocket to `/ws/activity`\n\n   Each has independent reconnection logic. If any one fails, that specific UI component shows stale data.\n\n3. **No Heartbeat/Health Check**: The WebSocket connections don't implement application-level heartbeats. TCP keepalives may not detect \"zombie\" connections where the server believes the client is connected but messages aren't flowing.\n\n**Architectural Justification:**\n- The component comments acknowledge the design: \"Falls back to placeholder if no WS yet\" (`ProgressChart.js:197`)\n- However, the fallback is just cached static data, not periodic re-fetching\n- ADR-001 states \"fault-tolerance and graceful degradation\" but the frontend implementation assumes happy-path WebSocket connectivity\n\n---\n\n## 4. Synthesis: Why the Delay is \"Intermittent\" and \"Worse Under Load\"\n\nThe reported symptoms\u2014**intermittent delays** that **worsen during peak hours**\u2014are classic indicators of an event-driven architecture under contention:\n\n1. **Kafka Consumer Lag Accumulation**: When message production rate exceeds consumption rate, lag grows. The notification-service queue group processes messages sequentially, so high-volume periods cause backlog.\n\n2. **Cache Serving Stale Data During High Load**: When many users are active:\n   - Cache hit rates increase (good for performance, bad for freshness)\n   - Invalidation patterns may miss edge cases\n   - New reads may hit recently-stale cache entries\n\n3. **WebSocket Infrastructure Bottlenecks**: Socket.IO server in notification-service handles all connected users. Under load:\n   - Room broadcasts (`io.to(userId).emit()`) may queue\n   - Memory pressure on the single service instance\n   - Docker network latency compounds\n\n4. **No End-to-End Backpressure**: The fire-and-forget event publishing means producers don't slow down when consumers are lagging. This allows the problem to compound.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Understanding of Architectural Trade-offs\n\nThis latency is **fundamentally a trade-off of the chosen loosely-coupled, event-driven architecture**. As documented in:\n\n- **ADR-001** (`001-microservices-architecture.md:72-75`): \"Data consistency becomes eventual; we must adopt Saga patterns for workflows\"\n- **ADR-002** (`002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md:65-68`): \"Learning curve \u2013 developers must understand eventual consistency\"\n- **ADR-003** (`003-polyglot-persistence.md:83-85`): \"Consumers materialize local read models, guaranteeing eventual consistency\"\n\nThe architecture **correctly prioritizes**:\n- Service autonomy and independent deployability\n- Fault isolation (course-service crash doesn't affect dashboard reads)\n- Horizontal scalability (add more consumers to reduce lag)\n\nThe architecture **trades away**:\n- Strong consistency guarantees\n- Instantaneous UI updates\n- Simplicity of data flow tracing\n\n**The 30-60 second delay is not a bug but an emergent property of the architectural choices under specific load conditions.** The system works \"correctly\"\u2014events are delivered eventually\u2014but user expectations for sub-second updates conflict with the eventual consistency model.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Summary of Findings\n\n| Bottleneck | Root Cause | Supporting Evidence |\n|------------|------------|---------------------|\n| **#1 Kafka Throughput** | Single broker, no partitioning | `docker-compose.yml:120-140`, `courseService.js:72-93` |\n| **#2 Cache Staleness** | 60s TTL, async invalidation | `courseService.js:101-109`, ADR-003 |\n| **#3 WebSocket Reliability** | No polling fallback, independent reconnection | `ProgressChart.js:139-151`, `DashboardPage.js:240-252` |\n\nThe combination of these factors explains why:\n- **Delays are intermittent**: Only occur when Kafka lag or cache staleness aligns with user action\n- **Worse under peak load**: Consumer lag grows non-linearly with event volume\n- **Up to 60 seconds**: Matches the cache TTL and max WebSocket reconnect interval\n\n---\n\n## 7. Appendix: File Reference Index\n\n| File | Path | Purpose |\n|------|------|---------|\n| Architecture Overview | `docs/architecture.md` | System design documentation |\n| ADR-001 | `docs/ADR/001-microservices-architecture.md` | Microservices decision |\n| ADR-002 | `docs/ADR/002-event-sourcing-with-kafka.md` | Event sourcing decision |\n| ADR-003 | `docs/ADR/003-polyglot-persistence.md` | Polyglot persistence decision |\n| Docker Compose | `docker-compose.yml` | Infrastructure configuration |\n| NGINX Config Builder | `services/api-gateway/nginx.conf` | API Gateway routing |\n| Course Service | `services/course-service/src/services/courseService.js` | Core business logic |\n| Course Controller | `services/course-service/src/api/courseController.js` | REST endpoints |\n| Event Producer | `services/course-service/src/events/producer.js` | NATS event publishing |\n| Course Repository | `services/course-service/src/repositories/courseRepository.js` | Data access |\n| Prisma Schema | `services/course-service/src/models/schema.prisma` | Database models |\n| Notification Service | `services/notification-service/src/server.js` | Event consumer + WebSocket |\n| Dashboard Page | `frontend/src/pages/DashboardPage.js` | Main dashboard component |\n| Progress Chart | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ProgressChart.js` | Real-time progress viz |\n| Activity Stream | `frontend/src/components/dashboard/ActivityStream.js` | Activity feed component |\n| Lecture Player | `frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js` | Video player + progress tracking |\n| Course Service (FE) | `frontend/src/services/courseService.js` | Frontend API client |\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/solution.md
# Architectural Analysis Report: User Progress Update Latency in PulseLearn Campus Hub

## Executive Summary

This report provides a root cause analysis of the intermittent latency (up to 60 seconds) users experience when their progress updates are reflected on the dashboard after completing course lectures or quizzes. After tracing the complete end-to-end data flow through the microservices architecture, I have identified that the primary cause is the **inherent eventual consistency** of the event-driven architecture, compounded by specific infrastructure and design choices that amplify latency under load.

---

## 1. Complete End-to-End Data Flow Trace

The user progress update flow involves two distinct pathways: a **synchronous write path** and an **asynchronous read path** with event propagation in between.

### 1.1 Synchronous Write Path (User Action to Database Persistence)

```
[User completes lecture]
    → [LecturePlayer.js]
    → [HTTP PUT/POST to API Gateway]
    → [NGINX reverse proxy]
    → [course-service Controller]
    → [courseService.js]
    → [PostgreSQL via Prisma]
    → [Kafka/NATS Event Published]
```

**Detailed Flow:**

1. **Frontend Trigger** (`frontend/src/components/course/LecturePlayer.js:181-189`):
   - When video playback ends, `handleEnded()` is called
   - Emits a `LectureCompleted` event via the client-side eventBus
   - Makes a synchronous POST to `/courses/${courseId}/lectures/${lectureId}/complete`
   - Also saves progress periodically via throttled PUT to `/courses/${courseId}/lectures/${lectureId}/progress` (every 5 seconds)

2. **API Gateway Routing** (`services/api-gateway/nginx.conf`):
   - NGINX proxies requests to upstream `content_service`
   - Rate limiting configured at 600 requests/minute per IP
   - Standard HTTP/1.1 prox
... (truncated)
